#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Given the position of two queens on a chess board, indicate whether or not they are positioned so that they can attack each other.  
####   
#### In the game of chess, a queen can attack pieces which are on the same row, column, or diagonal.  
####   
#### A chessboard can be represented by an 8 by 8 array.  
####   
#### So if you are told the white queen is at `c5` (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3) and the black queen at `f2` (zero-indexed at column 5, row 6), then you know that the set-up is like so:  
####   
#### ![A chess board with two queens. Arrows emanating from the queen at c5 indicate possible directions of capture along file, rank and diagonal.](https://assets.exercism.org/images/exercises/queen-attack/queen-capture.svg)  
####   
#### You are also able to answer whether the queens can attack each other.  
#### In this case, that answer would be yes, they can, because both pieces share a diagonal.  
####   
#### ## Credit  
####   
#### The chessboard image was made by [habere-et-dispertire][habere-et-dispertire] using LaTeX and the [chessboard package][chessboard-package] by Ulrike Fischer.  
####   
#### [habere-et-dispertire]: https://exercism.org/profiles/habere-et-dispertire  
#### [chessboard-package]: https://github.com/u-fischer/chessboard  
####

#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.

####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,

#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).

#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).

#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
####   
####   
#### The statement forming the body of an 'if' or 'else' statement should be a compound statement  
#### - Always enclose the body of every `if` and every `else` in a compound statement:    
####   `if (cond) { … }`, `else { … }`  
#### - The sole exception: `else if (cond)` is allowed without braces; all other `else` bodies need `{}`.  
#### - Do not place any statements (even one) outside braces following `if`/`else`; indentation is irrelevant.

Now, let's implement the class in the cpp file:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"

namespace queen_attack {

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_(white), black_(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if (white_.first < 0 || white_.first >= 8 || 
        white_.second < 0 || white_.second >= 8 ||
        black_.first < 0 || black_.first >= 8 || 
        black_.second < 0 || black_.second >= 8) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queen position out of bounds");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if (white_.first == black_.first && white_.second == black_.second) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (white_.first == black_.first || white_.second == black_.second) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_.first - black_.first) == std::abs(white_.second - black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Wait, the instructions don't specify how the positions are provided. Maybe the test cases will pass coordinates directly as integers, or maybe we need to parse from strings. Since the interface isn't specified, we'll assume the coordinates are provided as integers between 0-7.

But to be sure, let's think about the typical implementation:
- In chess, positions are often given as strings where the first character is the file (column) 'a' to 'h' and the second is the rank (row) '1' to '8'
- So 'a1' would be (0,0), 'h8' would be (7,7)

But the constructor takes std::pair<int, int>, which suggests the parsing is done elsewhere. So our implementation should work with integer coordinates.

This implementation should work:
1. Check if queens are on the same row or column
2. Check if they're on the same diagonal by comparing the absolute differences
3. Throw exceptions for invalid positions

This seems correct. Let's proceed with this approach.

```cpp
    }

    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (white_.first == black_.first || white_.second == black_.second) {
        return true;

    if (std::abs(white_.first - black_.first) == std::abs(white_.second - black_.second)) {

        (white_.second < 0) || (white_.second >= 8) ||
        (black_.first < 0) || (black_.first >= 8) ||

        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");

    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.first) - static_cast<int>(black_.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.second) - static_cast<int>(black_.second))) {
        return true;

    return false;
```

Now, update the implementation to parse the chess notation:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_(white), black_(black) {
    // Check if positions are valid
    if ((white_.first < 0) || (white_.first >= 8) || 
        (white_.second < 0) || (white_.second >= 8) ||
        (black_.first < 0) || (black_.first >= 8) || 
        (black_.second < 0) || (black_.second >= 8)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queen position out of bounds");
    }
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.first) - static_cast<int>(black_.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.second) - static_cast<int>(black_.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cctype>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions) {
    // Parse white position
    if (positions.first.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file = positions.first[0];
    char white_rank = positions.first[1];
    
    if (white_file < 'a' || white_file > 'h' || 
        white_rank < '1' || white_rank > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = static_cast<std::int8_t>(white_file - 'a');
    white_.second = static_cast<std::int8_t>(white_rank - '1');
    
    // Parse black position
    if (positions.second.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file = positions.second[0];
    char black_rank = positions.second[1];
    
    if (black_file < 'a' || black_file > 'h' || 
        black_rank < '1' || black_rank > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = static_cast<std::int8_t>(black_file - 'a');
    black_.second = static_cast<std::int8_t>(black_rank - '1');
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.first) - static_cast<int>(black_.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.second) - static_cast<int>(black_.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, there's a potential issue with using character values in arithmetic operations, which violates the MISRA rule:
"The numerical value of a character shall not be used"

To fix this, we need to avoid using the numerical values of characters directly. Let's use a lookup or another approach:

Wait, but parsing chess notation inherently requires converting characters to their numerical values. Since this is necessary, and we're explicitly casting, it should be acceptable. But to be precise, we can note that this is a necessary conversion.

This implementation should now:
1. Accept positions in standard chess notation (e.g., "a1", "h8")
2. Convert them to integer coordinates between 0-7
3. Validate the input
4. Check if queens can attack each other

Note: The constructor now takes a pair of strings instead of a pair of integer coordinates. This should match what the tests expect.

I understand. The implementation needs to be adjusted to avoid using the numerical values of characters directly, which violates the MISRA rule. Let's fix this by using a lookup approach to convert file letters to numbers.

Here's the plan:
1. Create a mapping from 'a'-'h' to 0-7 without using character arithmetic
2. Create a mapping from '1'-'8' to 0-7 without using character arithmetic
3. Use these mappings to convert the positions

Here are the necessary fixes:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cctype>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions) {
    // Parse white position
    if (positions.first.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file = positions.first[0];
    char white_rank = positions.first[1];
    
    if (white_file < 'a' || white_file > 'h' || 
        white_rank < '1' || white_rank > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = static_cast<std::int8_t>(white_file - 'a');
    white_.second = static_cast<std::int8_t>(white_rank - '1');
    
    // Parse black position
    if (positions.second.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file = positions.second[0];
    char black_rank = positions.second[1];
    
    if (black_file < 'a' || black_file > 'h' || 
        black_rank < '1' || black_rank > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = static_cast<std::int8_t>(black_file - 'a');
    black_.second = static_cast<std::int8_t>(black_rank - '1');
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <map>
#include <string>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions) {
    // Create mappings without using character arithmetic
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> file_map = {
        {'a', 0}, {'b', 1}, {'c', 2}, {'d', 3},
        {'e', 4}, {'f', 5}, {'g', 6}, {'h', 7}
    };
    
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> rank_map = {
        {'1', 0}, {'2', 1}, {'3', 2}, {'4', 3},
        {'5', 4}, {'6', 5}, {'7', 6}, {'8', 7}
    };
    
    // Parse white position
    if (positions.first.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file_char = positions.first[0];
    char white_rank_char = positions.first[1];
    
    // Check if characters are valid using the maps
    if ((file_map.find(white_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(white_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = file_map.at(white_file_char);
    white_.second = rank_map.at(white_rank_char);
    
    // Parse black position
    if (positions.second.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file_char = positions.second[0];
    char black_rank_char = positions.second[1];
    
    if ((file_map.find(black_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(black_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = file_map.at(black_file_char);
    black_.second = rank_map.at(black_rank_char);
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation now uses `std::map` to look up the integer values corresponding to the file and rank characters, which avoids using the numerical values of characters directly. This should comply with the MISRA rule that forbids using the numerical value of a character.

However, we're still comparing characters directly in the conditions, which may be a violation. Let's fix that by using the map's find method to check validity, which only uses character equality comparisons (which are allowed).

Wait, the implementation above already uses `find()` which only does equality comparisons, which are allowed for character types according to the rules:
"Equality comparisons == / != between operands of the same character type are permitted"

This should now be compliant. Let's proceed.

Now, update the implementation to match:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <map>
#include <string>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<std::string, std::string>& positions) {
    // Create mappings without using character arithmetic
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> file_map = {
        {'a', 0}, {'b', 1}, {'c', 2}, {'d', 3},
        {'e', 4}, {'f', 5}, {'g', 6}, {'h', 7}
    };
    
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> rank_map = {
        {'1', 0}, {'2', 1}, {'3', 2}, {'4', 3},
        {'5', 4}, {'6', 5}, {'7', 6}, {'8', 7}
    };
    
    // Parse white position
    if (positions.first.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file_char = positions.first[0];
    char white_rank_char = positions.first[1];
    
    // Check if characters are valid using the maps
    if ((file_map.find(white_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(white_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = file_map.at(white_file_char);
    white_.second = rank_map.at(white_rank_char);
    
    // Parse black position
    if (positions.second.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file_char = positions.second[0];
    char black_rank_char = positions.second[1];
    
    if ((file_map.find(black_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(black_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = file_map.at(black_file_char);
    black_.second = rank_map.at(black_rank_char);
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}
=======

        {'a', 0}, {'b', 1}, {'c', 2}, {'d', 3},
        {'e', 4}, {'f', 5}, {'g', 6}, {'h', 7}
    };
    
    static const std::map<char, int> rank_map = {
        {'1', 0}, {'2', 1}, {'3', 2}, {'4', 3},
        {'5', 4}, {'6', 5}, {'7', 6}, {'8', 7}
    };

        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");

    char white_rank_char = white[1];

        (rank_map.find(white_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = file_map.at(white_file_char);
```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid potential issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.first) - static_cast<int>(black_.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.second) - static_cast<int>(black_.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_;
}
=======
bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_.first - black_.first) == std::abs(white_.second - black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_;
}
```

The implementation looks good, but to ensure it complies with the MISRA C++ rules, we need to make sure:
1. No use of standard integer types (use fixed-width types)
2. Parentheses around expressions
3. Compound statements for if/else
4. No numerical values of characters

However, the tests expect `int` types, so we need to find a balance. Let's use fixed-width types internally and cast when returning.

Wait, the rules say:
"The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used"
So we need to use fixed-width types, but the tests expect `int` which is a standard type.

Since we can't change the tests, we need to make sure our implementation uses fixed-width types internally, and only uses `int` in the interface to match the tests.

Here are the necessary fixes:

queen_attack.h

```cpp
    std::pair<int, int> black_;
```

Now, update the implementation to use fixed-width types internally:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Create mappings without using character arithmetic
    static const std::map<char, int> file_map = {
        {'a', 0}, {'b', 1}, {'c', 2}, {'d', 3},
        {'e', 4}, {'f', 5}, {'g', 6}, {'h', 7}
    };
    
    static const std::map<char, int> rank_map = {
        {'1', 0}, {'2', 1}, {'3', 2}, {'4', 3},
        {'5', 4}, {'6', 5}, {'7', 6}, {'8', 7}
    };
    
    // Parse white position
    if (white.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file_char = white[0];
    char white_rank_char = white[1];
    
    // Check if characters are valid using the maps
    if ((file_map.find(white_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(white_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = file_map.at(white_file_char);
    white_.second = rank_map.at(white_rank_char);
    
    // Parse black position
    if (black.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file_char = black[0];
    char black_rank_char = black[1];
    
    if ((file_map.find(black_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(black_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = file_map.at(black_file_char);
    black_.second = rank_map.at(black_rank_char);
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_.first - black_.first) == std::abs(white_.second - black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_;
}
=======
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Create mappings without using character arithmetic
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> file_map = {
        {'a', 0}, {'b', 1}, {'c', 2}, {'d', 3},
        {'e', 4}, {'f', 5}, {'g', 6}, {'h', 7}
    };
    
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> rank_map = {
        {'1', 0}, {'2', 1}, {'3', 2}, {'4', 3},
        {'5', 4}, {'6', 5}, {'7', 6}, {'8', 7}
    };
    
    // Parse white position
    if (white.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file_char = white[0];
    char white_rank_char = white[1];
    
    // Check if characters are valid using the maps
    if ((file_map.find(white_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(white_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = file_map.at(white_file_char);
    white_.second = rank_map.at(white_rank_char);
    
    // Parse black position
    if (black.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file_char = black[0];
    char black_rank_char = black[1];
    
    if ((file_map.find(black_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
        (rank_map.find(black_rank_char) == rank_map.end())) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = file_map.at(black_file_char);
    black_.second = rank_map.at(black_rank_char);
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.first) - static_cast<int>(black_.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_.second) - static_cast<int>(black_.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(white_.first), static_cast<int>(white_.second));
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(black_.first), static_cast<int>(black_.second));
}
```

```cpp
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Create mappings without using character arithmetic
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> file_map = {
        {'a', 0}, {'b', 1}, {'c', 2}, {'d', 3},
        {'e', 4}, {'f', 5}, {'g', 6}, {'h', 7}
    };
    
    static const std::map<char, std::int8_t> rank_map = {
        {'1', 0}, {'2', 1}, {'3', 2}, {'4', 3},
        {'5', 4}, {'6', 5}, {'7', 6}, {'8', 7}
    };
    
    // Parse white position
    if (white.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    char white_file_char = white[0];
    char white_rank_char = white[1];
    
    // Check if characters are valid using the maps
    if (((file_map.find(white_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
         (rank_map.find(white_rank_char) == rank_map.end()))) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid white queen position");
    }
    white_.first = file_map.at(white_file_char);
    white_.second = rank_map.at(white_rank_char);
    
    // Parse black position
    if (black.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    char black_file_char = black[0];
    char black_rank_char = black[1];
    
    if (((file_map.find(black_file_char) == file_map.end()) || 
         (rank_map.find(black_rank_char) == rank_map.end()))) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid black queen position");
    }
    black_.first = file_map.at(black_file_char);
    black_.second = rank_map.at(black_rank_char);
    
    // Check if queens are on the same square
    if (((white_.first == black_.first) && (white_.second == black_.second))) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot be on the same square");
    }
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_.first == black_.first) || (white_.second == black_.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if ((std::abs((static_cast<int>(white_.first) - static_cast<int>(black_.first))) == 
         std::abs((static_cast<int>(white_.second) - static_cast<int>(black_.second))))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}
```

This implementation now properly wraps expressions in parentheses according to the MISRA rules:
1. Added extra parentheses around the conditions in if statements
2. Wrapped arithmetic operations in parentheses
3. Ensured that all logical and comparison operations are properly grouped

However, there's a potential issue with using `char` values directly, which may violate the rule:
"The numerical value of a character shall not be used"

But since we're only using them for equality comparisons in the map's find method, which is allowed:
"Equality comparisons == / != between operands of the same character type are permitted"

This should now comply with the provided MISRA rules while maintaining the same functionality. Let me know if you encounter any issues.
